Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 8c - High Voltage Overhead Lines
*************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1): "Authorized person" means an employee or agent:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(a): of a public utility that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(a)(i): generates, transmits, or delivers electricity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(a)(ii): provides and whose work relates to communication services;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(b): of an industrial plant whose work relates to the electrical system of the industrial plant;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(c): of a cable television or communication services company, or of a contractor of cable television or communication services company, if specifically and expressly authorized by the owner of the poles to make cable television or communication services attachments; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d): of a state, county, or municipal agency which has or whose work relates to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d)(i): overhead electrical lines;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d)(ii): overhead lighting systems;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d)(iii): authorized overhead circuit construction;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d)(iv): conductors on poles; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(1)(d)(v): structures of any type.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(2): "Business day" means any day other than Saturday, Sunday, or a legal holiday.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(3): "High voltage" means voltage in excess of 600 volts measured between:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(3)(a): conductors; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(3)(b): a conductor and the ground.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(4): "Overhead line" means all bare or insulated electrical conductors installed above the ground.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5): Title 54, Chapter 2, General Provisions; Title 10, Utah Municipal Code; Title 3, Uniform Agricultural Cooperative Association Act; 17B-1-102; Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act "Public utility" means any entity that generates, transmits, or distributes electrical energy, including any:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5)(a): Title 54, Chapter 2, General Provisions public utility as defined in
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5)(b): Title 10, Utah Municipal Code municipality as defined in
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5)(c): Title 3, Uniform Agricultural Cooperative Association Act agricultural cooperative association as defined in
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5)(d): 17B-1-102 improvement district as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(5)(e): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act entity created pursuant to
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-1(6): "Responsible party" means any person who contracts to perform, is responsible for the performance of, or has control over, any function or activity at any location.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2 Notification to public utility -- Protective measures -- Procedures -- Payment.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(1): No person or thing may be brought within 10 feet of any high voltage overhead line unless:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(1)(a): a responsible party has notified the public utility operating the high voltage overhead line of the intended activity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(1)(b): a responsible party and the public utility have completed mutually satisfactory precautions for the activity.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(2): 54-8c-6; (1)(a) If the identity of the public utility owning or operating the high voltage overhead line is unknown, the county clerk in the county where the line is located shall provide the name, address, and telephone number of the utility's designated representative.  If there is an association as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(3): (1)(b) Mutually satisfactory precautions required in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(3)(a): coordination of work, construction, and activity schedules;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(3)(b): placement of temporary mechanical barriers to separate and prevent contact between persons or things and the high voltage overhead line;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(3)(c): temporary deenergization and grounding or temporary relocation or raising of the high voltage overhead line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(4): If a responsible party is under contract or agreement with a governmental entity, and the governmental entity and the public utility operating the high voltage overhead line have already reached agreement concerning precautions, further agreements for the activity are not required.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(5): All responsible parties are obligated to pay to the public utility operating the high voltage overhead line the cost of mutually satisfactory precautions, except if:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(5)(a): prior arrangements for payment have been made between a governmental entity for whom the work is to be done and the public utility operating the line; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(5)(b): the public utility operating the line has not installed the line in conformance with the National Electrical Safety Code or its preceding code in effect at the time the line was constructed.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(6): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(6)(a): Unless other arrangements are necessary, the public utility operating the high voltage overhead line shall commence the precautionary measures:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(6)(a)(i): within three business days after the date an agreement for payment, if required, has been reached; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(6)(a)(ii): if no payment is required, within five business days after the date of the request of a responsible party.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-2(6)(b): The public utility shall not be required to provide the precautionary measures until an agreement for payment, if required, has been reached.  Once started, the precautionary measures shall continue without unreasonable interruption until completed.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3 Information filed with county clerk.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3(1): A public utility shall file with the county clerk of each county in which it has high voltage overhead lines a list containing:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3(1)(a): the name of the public utility owning the high voltage overhead lines;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3(1)(b): the name of any municipality, city, or town where the public utility operates high voltage overhead lines; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3(1)(c): the name, title, and address of its representative designated to receive calls for activity close to its high voltage overhead lines.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-3(2): 54-8c-6 In counties where an association provided in Section


Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4 Violation.
----------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4(1): Any responsible party who causes, permits, or allows a function or an activity in violation of any provision of this chapter is subject to a civil penalty in an amount not to exceed $1,000, to be imposed by any court of competent jurisdiction against this party and in favor of the state.  If imposed, the fine shall be paid into the General Fund.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4(2): Actions to recover the civil penalty under this section shall be brought by a public utility or the county attorney of the county in which the violation occurs.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4(3): A responsible party is liable to the public utility operating the high voltage overhead line for all damages to the facilities and for all liability incurred by the public utility as a result of any contact if:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4(3)(a): the responsible party causes, permits, or allows a function or an activity in violation of any provision of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-4(3)(b): as a result, a physical or electrical contact with a high voltage overhead line occurs.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-5 Exemptions.
-----------------------------------------
This chapter does not apply to construction, reconstruction, operation, or maintenance by an authorized person of:Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-5(1): overhead electrical, cable television, or communications circuits or conductors and their supporting structures;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-5(2): electrical generating, transmission, or distribution systems; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-5(3): communications, cable television, or overhead lighting systems.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6 Association for mutual receipt of notification of activities close to high voltage overhead lines.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(1): Public utilities may form and operate an association providing for mutual receipt of notification of activities close to high voltage overhead lines in a specified area.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2): 54-8c-2 In areas where an association is formed:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2)(a): 54-8c-2 notification to the association is effected as set forth in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2)(b): public utilities with high voltage overhead lines in the area:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2)(b)(i): may become members of the association;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2)(b)(ii): may participate in and receive the services furnished by the association; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(2)(b)(iii): shall pay their proportionate share of the cost for the services furnished.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(3): The association whose members or participants have high voltage overhead lines within a county shall file a list containing the name, address, and telephone number of every member and participating public utility with the county clerk.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-8c-6(4): If notification is made by telephone, an adequate record shall be maintained by the association to document compliance with the requirements of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 9 - Electric Power Facilities Act
**************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-101 Title.
-------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Electric Power Facilities Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102 Definitions.
-------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(1): "Common facilities" means all works and facilities:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(1)(a): owned or used by two or more public power entities or power utilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(1)(b): necessary to the generation, transmission, or distribution of electric power and energy.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(2): 11-13-103 "Interlocal entity" has the same meaning as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(3): 11-13-103 "Power utility":
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(3)(a): 11-13-103 means a public agency, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(3)(b): does not include a public power entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(4): "Public power entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(4)(a): a city or town that owns a system for the generation, transmission, or distribution of electric power and energy for public or private use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-102(4)(b): an interlocal entity.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103 Public power entity authority regarding common facilities -- Determination of needs -- Agreement requirements -- Ownership interest.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; 11-14-103(1)(b)(xi)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(a): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act; 11-14-103(1)(b)(xi) Notwithstanding
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(a)(i): plan, finance, construct, acquire, operate, own, and maintain an undivided interest in common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(a)(ii): participate in and enter into agreements with one or more public power entities or power utilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(a)(iii): enter into contracts and agreements as may be necessary or appropriate for the joint planning, financing, construction, operation, ownership, or maintenance of common facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(i): Before entering into an agreement providing for common facilities, the governing body of each public power entity shall determine the needs of the public power entity for electric power and energy based on engineering studies and reports.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii): In determining the future electric power and energy requirements of a public power entity, the governing body shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii)(A): the economies and efficiencies of scale to be achieved in constructing or acquiring common facilities for the generation and transmission of electric power and energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii)(B): the public power entity's need for reserve and peaking capacity, and to meet obligations under pooling and reserve sharing agreements reasonably related to the needs of the public power entity for power and energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii)(C): the estimated useful life of the common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii)(D): the estimated time necessary for the planning, financing, construction, and acquisition of the common facilities and the estimated timing of the need for an additional power supply; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(1)(b)(ii)(E): the reliability and availability of existing or alternate power supply sources and the cost of those existing or alternate power supply sources.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2): (2)(a)(i)(F); (2); (2)(a)(i)(I); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a): Each agreement providing for common facilities shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i): contain provisions not inconsistent with this chapter that the governing body of the public power entity determines to be in the interests of the public power entity, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(A): the purposes of the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(B): the duration of the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(C): the method of appointing or employing the personnel necessary in connection with the common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(D): the method of financing the common facilities, including the apportionment of costs of construction and operation;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(E): the ownership interests of the owners in the common facilities and other property used or useful in connection with the common facilities and the procedures for disposition of the common facilities and other property when the agreement expires or is terminated or when the common facilities are abandoned, decommissioned, or dismantled;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(F): any agreement of the parties prohibiting or restricting the alienation or partition of the undivided interests of an owner in the common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(G): the construction and repair of the common facilities, including, if the parties agree, a determination that a power utility or public power entity may construct or repair the common facilities as agent for all parties to the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(H): the administration, operation, and maintenance of the common facilities, including, if the parties agree, a determination that a power utility or public power entity may administer, operate, and maintain the common facilities as agent for all parties to the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(I): the creation of a committee of representatives of the parties to the agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(J): if the parties agree, a provision that if any party defaults in the performance or discharge of its obligations with respect to the common facilities, the other parties may perform or assume, pro rata or otherwise, the obligations of the defaulting party and may, if the defaulting party fails to remedy the default, succeed to or require the disposition of the rights and interests of the defaulting party in the common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(K): provisions for indemnification of construction, operation, and administration agents, for completion of construction, for handling emergencies, and for allocation of output of the common facilities among the parties to the agreement according to the ownership interests of the parties;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(L): methods for amending and terminating the agreement; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(i)(M): any other matter, not inconsistent with this chapter, determined by the parties to the agreement to be necessary and proper;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(ii): clearly disclose the ownership interest of each party;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(iii): provide for an equitable method of allocating operation, repair, and maintenance costs of the common facilities; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(a)(iv): be approved or ratified by resolution of the governing body of the public power entity.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(b): (2)(a)(i)(F); (2) A provision under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(c): (2)(a)(i)(I); (2) Each committee created under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(d): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(d)(i): The ownership interest of a public power entity in the common facilities may not be less than the proportion of the funds or the value of property supplied by it for the acquisition, construction, and operation of the common facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(2)(d)(ii): Each public power entity shall own and control the same proportion of the electrical output from the common facilities as its ownership interest in them.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-103(3): Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, an interlocal entity may not act in a manner inconsistent with any provision of the agreement under which it was created.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104 Joint owners to supply materials, arrange for own financing, and share in costs and taxes -- Public power entity authority to finance through financing agent -- Common facilities owners authority to appoint an agent.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(1): The joint owners of the common facilities shall supply the materials and make the payments provided for in the agreement.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(2): Each owner shall arrange its own funding and financing and be responsible for all the costs, interest, and payments required in connection with its share of the funding for the planning, acquisition, construction, operation, repairs, and improvements, and each participant shall pay its share of taxes or charges in lieu of taxes in connection with the common facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(3): Notwithstanding any other provision of this section, a public power entity may finance its funding share with one or more other owners through a financing agent, as long as no public power entity is liable for more than its proportionate share of the debt service with respect to the financing.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4): (4)(a); (3)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(a): The owners of common facilities may appoint as their agent:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(a)(i): a public power entity or power utility that owns an interest in common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(a)(ii): an interlocal entity of which a public power entity that owns an interest in the common facilities is a member;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(a)(iii): an interlocal entity that owns electric generation or transmission facilities that are located on a site adjacent to the common facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(a)(iv): a public agency that is an owner of the common facilities or that purchases power from a public agency that is an owner of the common facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(b): (4)(a); (3) One or more agents under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(b)(i): the construction, repair, administration, operation, or maintenance of the common facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(b)(ii): the administration and payment of, and any challenge or dispute regarding, any tax, fee in lieu of any tax, impact alleviation payment, or other fee or payment imposed by the state or a political subdivision of the state that relates to the common facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-104(4)(b)(iii): (3) the financing of all or part of the common facilities under Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105 Limitations on liability.
--------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(1): (1)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(1)(a): Each public power entity and power utility may be held liable only for its own acts, omissions, and obligations with respect to the planning, financing, construction, acquisition, administration, operation, ownership, repair, or maintenance of the common facilities and may not be jointly or severally liable for the acts, omissions, or obligations of others.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(1)(b): (1)(a) Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(1)(b)(i): affect the liability of a public power entity or power utility with respect to its contractual obligations, including a contractual obligation to indemnify a construction, operation, or administrative agent for the common facilities; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(1)(b)(ii): affect an immunity or other protection that may be available to a public power entity or power utility under applicable law.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(2): No money, materials, or other contribution supplied by a public power entity may be credited or otherwise applied to the account of any other owner in the common facilities, nor may the undivided share of a public power entity be charged, directly or indirectly, with any debt or obligation of any other owner or be subject to any lien as a result thereof.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-105(3): No action in connection with common facilities may be binding upon a public power entity unless the action or the agreement under which the action is taken is authorized or approved by a resolution or ordinance of its governing body.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106 Funding -- Power sales contracts -- Revenue bonds -- Fee in lieu of ad valorem property taxes -- Bond issues -- Public purpose.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(1): A public power entity participating in common facilities under this chapter may furnish money and provide property, both real and personal, and, in addition to any other authority now existing, may issue and sell, either at public or privately negotiated sale, general obligation bonds or revenue bonds, pledging either the revenues of its entire electric system or only its interest or share of the revenues derived from the common facilities in order to pay its respective share of the costs of the planning, financing, acquisition, construction, repair, and replacement of common facilities.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2): (2)(a); (2)(c); (2)(c)(ii)(A); (2)(c); 11-13-302

Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(b): (2)(a) Any revenues arising under a power sales contract under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c): (2)(c); (2)(c)(ii)(A); (2)(c); 11-13-302
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(i): (2)(c) As used in this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(ii): (2)(c)(ii)(A)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(ii)(A): Each power sales contract between a public power entity and a nonexempt purchaser shall contain a provision requiring the nonexempt purchaser to pay an annual fee to the public power entity in lieu of ad valorem property taxes.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(ii)(B): (2)(c)(ii)(A) The amount of the fee in lieu of ad valorem property taxes under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(iii): The public power entity shall pay over to the county treasurer each fee in lieu of ad valorem property taxes that it receives from a nonexempt purchaser for distribution in the same manner as other ad valorem tax revenues.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(2)(c)(iv): (2)(c); 11-13-302 This Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(3): A public power entity acquiring or owning an undivided interest in common facilities may contract with a county to pay, solely from the revenues derived from the interest of the public power entity in the common facilities, to the county or counties in which the common facilities are located, an annual fee in lieu of ad valorem property taxes based upon the taxable value of the percentage of the ownership share of the public power entity in the common facilities, which fee in lieu of ad valorem property taxes shall be paid over by the public power entity to the county treasurer of the county or counties in which the common facilities are located for distribution as per distribution of other ad valorem tax revenues.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(4): Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act; Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(4)(a): Title 11, Chapter 14, Local Government Bonding Act Bonds issued by a city or town shall be issued under the applicable provisions of
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(4)(b): Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act Bonds or other debt instruments issued by an interlocal entity shall be issued under
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-106(5): All money paid or property supplied by a public power entity for the purpose of carrying out powers conferred by this chapter is declared to be for a public purpose.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-107 Disposition of proceeds and revenues.
--------------------------------------------------------------------
All money belonging to a public power entity in connection with common facilities, including the proceeds of the sale of bonds and the revenues arising from the operation of common facilities:Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-107(1): may be deposited in a bank or trust company doing business within or without the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-107(2): shall be accounted for and disbursed in accordance with applicable law and the provisions of the resolution or indenture authorizing the issuance of the bonds.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-108 Scope -- Ownership or use of works or facilities.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-108(1): 11-13-101; Title 11, Chapter 13, Interlocal Cooperation Act Nothing in this chapter may be construed as imposing on an interlocal entity, as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-9-108(2): For purposes of this chapter, a person does not own or use works or facilities if the person is a party to a power sales contract to purchase output generated by, the capacity of, or an entitlement in the works or facilities.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 10a - Office of Consumer Services Act
******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-101 Title.
---------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Office of Consumer Services Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102 Definitions.
---------------------------------------------
For the purpose of this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(1): "Applicable public utility" means a public utility in this state for:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(1)(a): natural gas;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(1)(b): electricity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(1)(c): telephone.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(2): 54-10a-202 "Committee" means the Committee of Consumer Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(3): 54-10a-201 "Director" means the director of the office appointed under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(4): 54-10a-201 "Office" means the Office of Consumer Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(5): "Residential consumer" is a customer or user of an applicable public utility who maintains a permanent residence within the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(6): "Small commercial consumer" is a person conducting a business enterprise, agriculture enterprise, or other enterprise in the state that has:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(6)(a): less than 25 employees; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-102(6)(b): a gross income less than $1,000,000 annually.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201 Office of Consumer Services -- Director.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(1): There is created within the Department of Commerce the "Office of Consumer Services."
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(2)(a): The governor shall appoint, with the concurrence of the Committee of Consumer Services and the advice and consent of the Senate, a qualified person in the field of public utilities to be the director of the office.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(2)(b): The director shall serve for a term of six years.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(2)(c): For purposes of the individual who is the director on May 12, 2009, that individual's six-year term is considered to begin on July 1, 2009.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(2)(d): The governor may remove the director for cause.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(3): In accordance with this chapter, the director shall on behalf of the office:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(3)(a): represent residential consumers and small commercial consumers of an applicable public utility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(3)(b): represent the interests of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(3)(b)(i): residential consumers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-10a-201(3)(b)(ii): small commercial consumers.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 12 - Small Power Production and Cogeneration
*************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-1 Legislative policy.
-------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-1(1): The Legislature declares that in order to promote the more rapid development of new sources of electrical energy, to maintain the economic vitality of the state through the continuing production of goods and the employment of its people, and to promote the efficient utilization and distribution of energy, it is desirable and necessary to encourage independent energy producers to competitively develop sources of electric energy not otherwise available to Utah businesses, residences, and industries served by electrical corporations, and to remove unnecessary barriers to energy transactions involving independent energy producers and electrical corporations.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-1(2): It is the policy of this state to encourage the development of independent and qualifying power production and cogeneration facilities, to promote a diverse array of economical and permanently sustainable energy resources in an environmentally acceptable manner, and to conserve our finite and expensive energy resources and provide for their most efficient and economic utilization.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-2 Purchase of power from qualifying power producers.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-2(1): Purchasing utilities shall offer to purchase power from qualifying power producers.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-2(2): The commission shall establish reasonable rates, terms, and conditions for the purchase or sale of electricity or electrical generating capacity, or both, between a purchasing utility and a qualifying power producer.  In establishing these rates, terms, and conditions, the commission shall either establish a procedure under which qualifying power producers offer competitive bids for the sale of power to purchasing utilities or devise an alternative method which considers the purchasing utility's avoided costs.  The capacity component of avoided costs shall reflect the purchasing utility's long-term deferral or cancellation of generating units which may result from the purchase of power from qualifying power producers.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-2(3): (2) Purchasing utilities and qualifying power producers may agree to rates, terms, or conditions for the sale of electricity or electrical capacity which differ from the rates, terms, and conditions adopted by the commission under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-2(4): The commission may adopt further rules which encourage the development of small power production and cogeneration facilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-12-3 Recovery of investment costs.
-----------------------------------------------------------
The commission may not consider any purchasing utility's purchase of power from a qualifying power producer as a reason for disallowing recovery of the purchasing utility's investment costs for facilities which are in use prior to signing a contract for the purchase of power from a qualifying power producer.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 13 - Natural Gas Pipeline Safety
*************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-1 Definitions.
------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter, "intrastate pipeline transportation" and "pipeline facilities" have the definitions set forth in the Natural Gas Pipeline Safety Act of 1968, 49 U.S.C.  Section 60101.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-2 Commission's responsibilities.
------------------------------------------------------------
The commission is responsible for establishing safety standards and practices for intrastate pipeline transportation and shall make and enforce rules required by the federal Natural Gas Pipeline Safety Act to maintain state control over the regulation of intrastate pipeline transportation.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-3 Rules.
------------------------------------
The commission shall adopt and enforce rules pursuant to SectionUtah Code Annotated § 54-13-3(1): incorporate the safety standards established under the federal Natural Gas Pipeline Safety Act that are applicable to intrastate pipeline transportation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-3(2): require persons engaged in intrastate pipeline transportation to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-3(2)(a): maintain records and to submit reports and information to the commission to enable the commission to determine whether the person is acting in compliance with this chapter or rules adopted under this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-3(2)(b): maintain a plan for inspection and maintenance of each pipeline facility that is available to the commission upon commission request.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-4 Inspection and examination of records and properties.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Officers, employees, or agents authorized by the commission, upon presenting appropriate credentials to the person in charge, may inspect and examine, at reasonable times and in a reasonable manner, the records and properties of any person engaged in intrastate pipeline transportation to the extent those records and properties are relevant to determining whether the person is acting in compliance with this chapter or rules under this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-5 Establishment of fee.
---------------------------------------------------
The commission may, by rule, establish a fee for the inspection of pipeline facilities of any person engaged in intrastate pipeline transportation who does not pay a public utilities regulation fee pursuant to

Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8 Violation of chapter -- Penalty.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(1): Any person engaged in intrastate pipeline transportation who is determined by the commission, after notice and an opportunity for a hearing, to have violated any provision of this chapter or any rule or order issued under this chapter, is liable for a civil penalty of not more than $100,000 for each violation for each day the violation persists.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(2): The maximum civil penalty assessed under this section may not exceed $1,000,000 for any related series of violations.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(3): The amount of the penalty shall be assessed by the commission by written notice.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4): In determining the amount of the penalty, the commission shall consider:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(a): the nature, circumstances, and gravity of the violation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b): with respect to the person found to have committed the violation:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(i): the degree of culpability;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(ii): any history of prior violations;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(iii): the effect on the person's ability to continue to do business;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(iv): any good faith in attempting to achieve compliance;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(v): the person's ability to pay the penalty; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(4)(b)(vi): any other matter, as justice may require.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(5)(a): A civil penalty assessed under this section may be recovered in an action brought by the attorney general on behalf of the state in the appropriate district court, or before referral to the attorney general, it may be compromised by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(5)(b): The amount of the penalty, when finally determined, or agreed upon in compromise, may be deducted from any sum owed by the state to the person charged.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-13-8(6): Any penalty collected under this section shall be deposited in the General Fund.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 14 - Utility Facility Review Board Act
*******************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Utility Facility Review Board Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102 Legislative findings.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102(1)(a): The Legislature finds that the construction of facilities by public utilities under this title is a matter of statewide concern.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102(1)(b): The construction of these facilities may affect the safety, reliability, adequacy, and efficiency of service to customers in areas within the jurisdiction of more than a single local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102(1)(c): Excess costs imposed by requirements of a local government for the construction of facilities may affect either the rates and charges of the public utility to customers other than customers within the jurisdiction of the local government or the financial viability of the public utility, unless the local government pays for those excess costs.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-102(2): The Legislature finds that it is in the public interest to establish the Utility Facility Review Board to resolve issues regarding the construction and installation of public utility facilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(1): 54-14-203 "Actual excess cost" means the difference in cost between:

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(1)(b): 54-14-203 the actual cost of the facility, including any necessary right-of-way, as determined in accordance with Section

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(3): "Commencement of construction of a facility" includes the project design and the ordering of materials necessary to construct the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(4): "Estimated excess cost" means any material difference in estimated cost between the costs of a facility, including any necessary right-of-way, if constructed in accordance with the requirements of a local government and the standard cost of the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(5): 54-18-102

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(6):

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(6)(a)(i): pipe;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(6)(a)(ii): a compressor;

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-103(10)(a)(iii): the structure intended to restrict access to the equipment to qualified persons.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-104 Rules and procedures.
-----------------------------------------------------
The board may, pursuant to

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-201 Conditions on siting of facilities by local governments -- Payment of actual excess costs.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If otherwise authorized by law, a local government may require or condition the construction of a facility in any manner if:Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-201(1): the requirements or conditions do not impair the ability of the public utility to provide safe, reliable, and adequate service to its customers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-201(2): the local government pays for the actual excess cost resulting from the requirements or conditions, except:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-201(2)(a): any actual excess costs that the public utility collects from its customers pursuant to an order, rule, or regulation of the commission; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-201(2)(b): any portion of the actual excess costs that the board requires to be borne by the public utility.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-203 Actual excess cost.
---------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-203(1): If a local government issues a permit, authorization, approval, exception, or waiver based upon its agreement to pay for the actual excess cost of a facility, the local government shall within 30 days either accept the estimate of excess cost as the actual excess cost of a facility or request the public utility to obtain competitive bids for the facility if constructed in accordance with the requirements and conditions of the local government.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-203(2): If the local government requests the public utility to obtain competitive bids, the public utility shall obtain competitive bids, and the actual excess cost of the facility shall be the difference between the lowest bid acceptable to the public utility plus the public utility's contract administration and oversight expense and the standard cost of the facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-203(3): Any dispute regarding specifications, lowest acceptable bid, or administration and oversight expense shall be resolved by the board on an expedited basis.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-204 Requirements or conditions on facility considered waived if local government does not pay for actual excess cost 30 days before construction.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Any requirement or condition in any permit, authorization, approval, exception, or waiver of a local government for a facility that imposes an actual excess cost shall be considered waived if the local government does not pay the public utility for the actual excess cost, except any actual excess costs specified in Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301 Creation, purpose, and composition of board.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(1): The Utility Facility Review Board is created to resolve disputes between local governments and public utilities regarding the siting and construction of facilities as provided in this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(2): The board shall be composed of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(2)(a): the three members of the commission;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(2)(b): an individual appointed by the governor from a list of nominees of the Utah League of Cities and Towns; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(2)(c): an individual appointed by the governor from a list of nominees of the Utah Association of Counties.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(3): The chair of the commission shall serve as chair of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(4): Members of the commission shall serve as members of the board during their terms of office as commissioners and until their successors on the commission have been appointed and taken office.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5)(a): Members of the board who are not commissioners:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5)(a)(i): shall have four-year terms, except the initial term of the individual first appointed by the governor from nominees of the Utah Association of Counties shall be two years;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5)(a)(ii): may be appointed for one succeeding term; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5)(a)(iii): may continue to serve until their successor takes office.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(5)(b): Vacancies in the board of members who are not commissioners shall be filled for the unexpired term.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(6): Three members of the board constitute a quorum.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(7): A member of the board may be removed for cause by the governor.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(8): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107; 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 A member may not receive compensation or benefits for the member's service, but may receive per diem and travel expenses in accordance with:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(8)(a): 63A-3-106 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(8)(b): 63A-3-107 Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-301(8)(c): 63A-3-106; 63A-3-107 rules made by the Division of Finance pursuant to Sections


Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-302 Staff and support for board.
------------------------------------------------------------
The Department of Commerce and the commission shall provide any staff, services, or meeting rooms the board requires to perform its duties.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304 Initial hearing.
------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304(1): The board shall convene an initial hearing within 50 days after the date review is initiated.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304(2): At the initial hearing, the board shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304(2)(a): determine how the review will take place, including whether it will be conducted as a formal or informal adjudicative proceeding; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304(2)(b): set a schedule for the review proceeding.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-304(3): The board shall hold a hearing on the merits within 60 days after the initial hearing.

-----------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-305(1): The board shall issue a written decision on the review expeditiously and, in any event, not later than 75 days following the initial hearing.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306 Action required of local government following board decision.
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306(1): If the board decides that a facility permitted to be constructed by a local government is subject to requirements or conditions that impose an estimated excess cost but do not impair the provision of safe, reliable, and adequate service to customers of the public utility, the local government shall, within 20 days following the decision of the board, determine whether it will impose the requirement or conditions imposing an estimated excess cost or issue the permit, authorization, approval, exception, or waiver without the requirements or conditions imposing an estimated excess cost.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306(2): If the board decides that a facility should be constructed that the local government has prohibited, the local government shall, within 60 days following the decision of the board, issue the permit, authorization, approval, exception, or waiver consistent with the decision of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306(3): (1); (2); 54-14-201(2)(a); (2)(b) The local government may impose requirements or conditions pursuant to its zoning, subdivision, or building code regulations if:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306(3)(a): the requirements or conditions do not impair safe, reliable, and adequate service to the customers of the utility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-306(3)(b): (1); (2); 54-14-201(2)(a); (2)(b) the local government enters into an agreement with the public utility within the 20-day time limit specified by Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-307 Stay of board's decision pending review or appeal.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-307(1): A petition for review, rehearing, or reconsideration or a petition for judicial review does not stay or suspend the effectiveness of a written decision of the board.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-307(2): 63G-4-405 Any party seeking to stay the effectiveness of a decision of the board shall seek a stay under Section


Utah Code Annotated § 54-14-308 Judicial review in formal adjudicative proceedings.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The Court of Appeals has jurisdiction to review any decision of the board in a formal adjudicative proceeding.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 15 - Net Metering of Electricity
*************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Net Metering of Electricity."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(1): "Annualized billing period" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(1)(a): a 12-month billing cycle beginning on April 1 of one year and ending on March 31 of the following year; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(1)(b): an additional 12-month billing cycle as defined by an electrical corporation's net metering tariff or rate schedule.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(2): "Customer-generated electricity" means electricity that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(2)(a): is generated by a customer generation system for a customer participating in a net metering program;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(2)(b): exceeds the electricity the customer needs for the customer's own use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(2)(c): is supplied to the electrical corporation administering the net metering program.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3): "Customer generation system":
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a): means an eligible facility that is used to supply energy to or for a specific customer that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(i): has a generating capacity of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(i)(A): not more than 25 kilowatts for a residential facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(i)(B): not more than two megawatts for a non-residential facility, unless the governing authority approves a greater generation capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(ii): is located on, or adjacent to, the premises of the electrical corporation's customer, subject to the electrical corporation's service requirements;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(iii): operates in parallel and is interconnected with the electrical corporation's distribution facilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(iv): is intended primarily to offset part or all of the customer's requirements for electricity; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(a)(v): is controlled by an inverter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(3)(b): includes an electric generator and its accompanying equipment package.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4): "Eligible facility" means a facility that uses energy derived from one of the following to generate electricity:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(a): solar photovoltaic and solar thermal energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(b): wind energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(c): hydrogen;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(d): organic waste;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(e): hydroelectric energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(f): waste gas and waste heat capture or recovery;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(g): biomass and biomass byproducts, except for the combustion of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(g)(i): wood that has been treated with chemical preservatives such as creosote, pentachlorophenol, or chromated copper arsenate; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(g)(ii): municipal waste in a solid form;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(h): forest or rangeland woody debris from harvesting or thinning conducted to improve forest or rangeland ecological health and to reduce wildfire risk;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(i): agricultural residues;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(j): dedicated energy crops;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(k): landfill gas or biogas produced from organic matter, wastewater, anaerobic digesters, or municipal solid waste; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(4)(l): geothermal energy.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(5): "Equipment package" means a group of components connecting an electric generator to an electric distribution system, including all interface equipment and the interface equipment's controls, switchgear, inverter, and other interface devices.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(6): "Excess customer-generated electricity" means the amount of customer-generated electricity in excess of the customer's consumption from the customer generation system during a monthly billing period, as measured at the electrical corporation's meter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(7): "Fuel cell" means a device in which the energy of a reaction between a fuel and an oxidant is converted directly and continuously into electrical energy.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(8): "Governing authority" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(8)(a): for a distribution electrical cooperative, its board of directors; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(8)(b): for each other electrical corporation, the Public Service Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(9): "Inverter" means a device that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(9)(a): converts direct current power into alternating current power that is compatible with power generated by an electrical corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(9)(b): has been designed, tested, and certified to UL1741 and installed and operated in accordance with the latest revision of IEEE1547, as amended.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(10): "Net electricity" means the difference, as measured at the meter owned by the electrical corporation between:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(10)(a): the amount of electricity that an electrical corporation supplies to a customer participating in a net metering program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(10)(b): the amount of customer-generated electricity delivered to the electrical corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(11): "Net metering" means measuring the amount of net electricity for the applicable billing period.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(12): 54-15-104 "Net metering program" means a program administered by an electrical corporation whereby a customer with a customer generation system may:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(12)(a): generate electricity primarily for the customer's own use;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(12)(b): supply customer-generated electricity to the electrical corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(12)(c): 54-15-104 if net metering results in excess customer-generated electricity during a billing period, receive a credit as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13): "Switchgear" means the combination of electrical disconnects, fuses, or circuit breakers:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(a): used to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(a)(i): isolate electrical equipment; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(a)(ii): de-energize equipment to allow work to be performed or faults downstream to be cleared; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(b): that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(b)(i): designed, tested, and certified to UL1741; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-102(13)(b)(ii): installed and operated in accordance with the latest revision of IEEE1547, as amended.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104 Charges or credits for net electricity.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(1): Each electrical corporation with a customer participating in a net metering program shall measure net electricity during each monthly billing period, in accordance with normal metering practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(2): If net metering does not result in excess customer-generated electricity during the monthly billing period, the electrical corporation shall bill the customer for the net electricity, in accordance with normal billing practices.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(3): (4) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(3)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(3)(a)(i): the electrical corporation shall credit the customer for the excess customer-generated electricity based on the meter reading for the billing period at a value that is at least avoided cost, or as determined by the governing authority; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(3)(a)(ii): all credits that the customer does not use during the annualized billing period expire at the end of the annualized billing period; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(3)(b): as authorized by the governing authority, the electrical corporation may bill the customer for customer charges that otherwise would have accrued during that billing period in the absence of excess customer-generated electricity.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(4): (3)(a) At the end of an annualized billing period, an electrical corporation's avoided cost value of remaining unused credits described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(4)(a): to the electrical corporation's low-income assistance programs as determined by the governing authority; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-104(4)(b): for another use as determined by the governing authority.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-105.1 Determination of costs and benefits -- Determination of just and reasonable charge, credit, or ratemaking structure.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
The governing authority shall:Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-105.1(1): determine, after appropriate notice and opportunity for public comment, whether costs that the electrical corporation or other customers will incur from a net metering program will exceed the benefits of the net metering program, or whether the benefits of the net metering program will exceed the costs; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-105.1(2): determine a just and reasonable charge, credit, or ratemaking structure, including new or existing tariffs, in light of the costs and benefits.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106 Customer to provide equipment necessary to meet certain requirements -- Governing authority may adopt additional reasonable requirements -- Testing and inspection of interconnection.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act Each customer participating in a net metering program shall provide at the customer's expense all equipment necessary to meet:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(1)(a): applicable local and national standards regarding electrical and fire safety, power quality, and interconnection requirements established by the National Electrical Code, the National Electrical Safety Code, the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers, and Underwriters Laboratories; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(1)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act any other utility interconnection requirements as determined by the commission by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(2): After appropriate notice and opportunity for public comment, the governing authority may by rule adopt additional reasonable safety, power quality, and interconnection requirements for customer generation systems that the governing authority considers to be necessary to protect public safety and system reliability.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(3): (1); (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(3)(a): (1); (2) If a customer participating in a net metering program complies with requirements referred to under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(3)(a)(i): perform or pay for additional tests; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(3)(a)(ii): purchase additional liability insurance.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(3)(b): An electrical corporation may not be held directly or indirectly liable for permitting or continuing to permit an interconnection of a customer generation system to the electrical corporation's system or for an act or omission of a customer participating in a net metering program for loss, injury, or death to a third party.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(4): An electrical corporation may test and inspect an interconnection at times that the electrical corporation considers necessary to ensure the safety of electrical workers and to preserve the integrity of the electric power grid.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-106(5): The electrical function, operation, or capacity of a customer generation system, at the point of connection to the electrical corporation's distribution system, may not compromise the quality of service to the electrical corporation's other customers.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-107 Application to out-of-state electrical corporation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------
An electrical corporation with fewer than 5,000 customers in this state that is headquartered in another state is considered to be in compliance with this chapter if the electrical corporation offers net metering to its customers in Utah in accordance with a tariff, schedule, or other requirement of the appropriate authority in the state in which the electrical corporation's headquarters are located.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-108 Damages and fines for connecting a customer generation system to more than one customer.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
If an independent energy producer that is supplying energy to a customer described in SubsectionUtah Code Annotated § 54-15-108(1): award damages to an electrical corporation for actual and consequential damages to the electrical corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-15-108(2): assess a fine against the independent energy producer or person responsible for the violation.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 17 - Energy Resource Procurement Act
*****************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Energy Resource Procurement Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(1): "Affected electrical utility" means an electrical corporation with at least 200,000 retail customers in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2): "Benchmark option" means an energy resource against which bids in an open bid process may be evaluated that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(a): could be constructed or owned by:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(a)(i): an affected electrical utility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(a)(ii): an affiliate of an affected electrical utility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(b): may be a purchase of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(b)(i): electricity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(b)(ii): electric generating capacity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(2)(b)(iii): electricity and electric generating capacity.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3): "Integrated resource plan" means a plan that contains:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(a): the demand and energy forecast by the affected electrical utility for at least a ten-year period;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(b): the affected electrical utility's options for meeting the requirements shown in its load and resource forecast in an economic and reliable manner, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(b)(i): demand-side and supply-side options; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(b)(ii): a brief description and summary cost-benefit analysis, if available, of each option that was considered;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(c): the affected electrical utility's assumptions and conclusions with respect to the effect of the plan on the cost and reliability of energy service;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(d): a description of the external environmental and economic consequences of the plan to the extent practicable; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(3)(e): any other data and analyses as the commission may require.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act "Significant energy resource" for an affected electrical utility means a resource that consists of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(a): a total of 100 megawatts or more of new generating capacity that has a dependable life of 10 or more years;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(b): a purchase of the following if the contract is for a term of 10 or more years and not less than 100 megawatts:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(b)(i): electricity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(b)(ii): electric generating capacity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(b)(iii): electricity and electrical generating capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(c): the purchase or lease by an affected electrical utility from an affiliated company of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(c)(i): a generating facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(c)(ii): electricity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(c)(iii): electrical generating capacity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(c)(iv): electricity and electrical generating capacity;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(d): a contract with an option for the affected electrical utility or an affiliate to purchase a resource that consists of not less than 100 megawatts or more of new generating capacity that has a remaining dependable life of 10 or more years; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(4)(e): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act a type of resource designated by the commission as a significant energy resource in rules made by the commission in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-102(5): "Solicitation" means a request for proposals or other invitation for persons to submit a bid or proposal through an open bid process for construction or acquisition of a significant energy resource.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401 Definitions -- Rules.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1): As used in this part:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(a): "Energy utility" means one of the following with 200,000 retail customers in the state:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(a)(i): an electrical corporation; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(a)(ii): a gas corporation.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b): "Resource decision" means a decision, other than a decision to construct or acquire a significant energy resource, involving:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b)(i): an energy utility's acquisition, management, or operation of energy production, processing, transmission, or distribution facilities or processes including:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b)(i)(A): a facility or process for the efficient, reliable, or safe provision of energy to retail customers;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b)(i)(B): an energy efficiency and conservation program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b)(i)(C): rural gas infrastructure development; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(b)(ii): a decision determined by the commission to be appropriate for review under this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(1)(c): "Rural gas infrastructure development" means the acquisition, planning, development, extension, expansion, and construction of natural gas utility facilities to serve previously unserved rural areas of the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-401(2): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act; 54-17-402 The commission may adopt rules in accordance with


Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402 Request for review of resource decision.
------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(1): Beginning on February 25, 2005, before implementing a resource decision, an energy utility may request that the commission approve all or part of a resource decision in accordance with this part.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2): (1); Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(a): (1) To obtain the approval permitted by Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(b): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act The request for approval required by this section shall include any information required by the commission by rule made in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(c): A request for approval of natural gas infrastructure development shall include:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(c)(i): a description of the proposed rural gas infrastructure development project;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(c)(ii): an explanation of projected benefits from the proposed rural gas infrastructure development project;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(c)(iii): the estimated costs of the rural gas infrastructure development project; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(2)(c)(iv): any other information the commission requires.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-402(3): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In ruling on a request for approval of a resource decision, the commission shall determine whether the decision:

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1): 54-17-602(1); 54-7-12.8; 54-17-603(4)(b) "Adjusted retail electric sales" means the total kilowatt-hours of retail electric sales of an electrical corporation to customers in this state in a calendar year, reduced by:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(a): the amount of those kilowatt-hours attributable to electricity generated or purchased in that calendar year from qualifying zero carbon emissions generation and qualifying carbon sequestration generation;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b): 54-17-602(1) the amount of those kilowatt-hours attributable to electricity generated or purchased in that calendar year from generation located within the geographic boundary of the Western Electricity Coordinating Council that derives its energy from one or more of the following but that does not satisfy the definition of a renewable energy source or that otherwise has not been used to satisfy Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(i): wind energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(ii): solar photovoltaic and solar thermal energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iii): wave, tidal, and ocean thermal energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv): except for combustion of wood that has been treated with chemical preservatives such as creosote, pentachlorophenol or chromated copper arsenate, biomass and biomass byproducts, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv)(A): organic waste;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv)(B): forest or rangeland woody debris from harvesting or thinning conducted to improve forest or rangeland ecological health and to reduce wildfire risk;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv)(C): agricultural residues;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv)(D): dedicated energy crops; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(iv)(E): landfill gas or biogas produced from organic matter, wastewater, anaerobic digesters, or municipal solid waste;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(v): geothermal energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(vi): hydroelectric energy; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(b)(vii): waste gas and waste heat capture or recovery; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(1)(c): 54-7-12.8; 54-17-603(4)(b) the number of kilowatt-hours attributable to reductions in retail sales in that calendar year from demand side management as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(2): "Amount of kilowatt-hours attributable to electricity generated or purchased in that calendar year from qualifying carbon sequestration generation," for qualifying carbon sequestration generation, means the kilowatt-hours supplied by a facility during the calendar year multiplied by the ratio of the amount of carbon dioxide captured from the facility and sequestered to the sum of the amount of carbon dioxide captured from the facility and sequestered plus the amount of carbon dioxide emitted from the facility during the same calendar year.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(3): "Banked renewable energy certificate" means a bundled or unbundled renewable energy certificate that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(3)(a): not used in a calendar year to comply with this part or with a renewable energy program in another state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(3)(b): carried forward into a subsequent year.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(4): "Bundled renewable energy certificate" means a renewable energy certificate for qualifying electricity that is acquired:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(4)(a): by an electrical corporation by a trade, purchase, or other transfer of electricity that includes the renewable energy attributes of, or certificate that is issued for, the electricity; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(4)(b): by an electrical corporation by generating the electricity for which the renewable energy certificate is issued.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(5): 54-2-1 "Electrical corporation":
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(5)(a): 54-2-1 is as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(5)(b): does not include a person generating electricity that is not for sale to the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(6): "Qualifying carbon sequestration generation" means a fossil-fueled generating facility located within the geographic boundary of the Western Electricity Coordinating Council that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(6)(a): becomes operational or is retrofitted on or after January 1, 2008; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(6)(b): reduces carbon dioxide emissions into the atmosphere through permanent geological sequestration or through another verifiably permanent reduction in carbon dioxide emissions through the use of technology.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(7): "Qualifying electricity" means electricity generated on or after January 1, 1995 from a renewable energy source if:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(7)(a): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(7)(a)(i): the renewable energy source is located within the geographic boundary of the Western Electricity Coordinating Council; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(7)(a)(ii): the qualifying electricity is delivered to the transmission system of an electrical corporation or a delivery point designated by the electrical corporation for the purpose of subsequent delivery to the electrical corporation; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(7)(b): the renewable energy attributes of the electricity are not traded, sold, transferred, or otherwise used to satisfy another state's renewable energy program.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8): 54-17-602(1) "Qualifying zero carbon emissions generation":
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8)(a): means a generation facility located within the geographic boundary of the Western Electricity Coordinating Council that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8)(a)(i): becomes operational on or after January 1, 2008; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8)(a)(ii): does not produce carbon as a byproduct of the generation process;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8)(b): includes generation powered by nuclear fuel; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(8)(c): 54-17-602(1) does not include renewable energy sources used to satisfy the requirement established under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(9): 54-17-603 "Renewable energy certificate" means a certificate issued under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(10): (10)(a); (b); (10)(a); (c); 54-7-12.8(1) "Renewable energy source" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(10)(a): an electric generation facility or generation capability or upgrade that becomes operational on or after January 1, 1995 that derives its energy from one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-601(10)(a)(i): wind energy;
