Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701 Rules for carbon capture and geological storage.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1): By January 1, 2011, the Division of Water Quality and the Division of Air Quality, on behalf of the Board of Water Quality and the Board of Air Quality, respectively, in collaboration with the commission and the Division of Oil, Gas, and Mining and the Utah Geological Survey, shall present recommended rules to the Legislature's Administrative Rules Review and General Oversight Committee for the following in connection with carbon capture and accompanying geological sequestration of captured carbon:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(a): site characterization approval;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(b): geomechanical, geochemical, and hydrogeological simulation;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(c): risk assessment;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(d): mitigation and remediation protocols;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(e): issuance of permits for test, injection, and monitoring wells;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(f): specifications for the drilling, construction, and maintenance of wells;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(g): issues concerning ownership of subsurface rights and pore space;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(h): allowed composition of injected matter;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(i): testing, monitoring, measurement, and verification for the entirety of the carbon capture and geologic sequestration chain of operations, from the point of capture of the carbon dioxide to the sequestration site;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(j): closure and decommissioning procedure;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(k): short- and long-term liability and indemnification for sequestration sites;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(l): conversion of enhanced oil recovery operations to carbon dioxide geological sequestration sites; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(1)(m): other issues as identified.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(2): (1); (1) The entities listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(3): (1) On or before July 1, 2009, the entities listed in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(4): The recommended rules developed under this section apply to the injection of carbon dioxide and other associated injectants in allowable types of geological formations for the purpose of reducing emissions to the atmosphere through long-term geological sequestration as required by law or undertaken voluntarily or for subsequent beneficial reuse.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(5): The recommended rules developed under this section do not apply to the injection of fluids through the use of Class II injection wells as defined in 40 C.F.R. 144.6(b) for the purpose of enhanced hydrocarbon recovery.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(6): Rules recommended under this section shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(6)(a): ensure that adequate health and safety standards are met;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(6)(b): minimize the risk of unacceptable leakage from the injection well and injection zone for carbon capture and geologic sequestration; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-701(6)(c): provide adequate regulatory oversight and public information concerning carbon capture and geologic sequestration.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(1): "Contract customer" means a person who executes or will execute a renewable energy contract with a qualified utility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(2): "Qualified utility" means an electric corporation that serves more than 200,000 retail customers in the state.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(3): "Renewable energy contract" means a contract under this part for the delivery of electricity from one or more renewable energy facilities to a contract customer requiring the use of a qualified utility's transmission or distribution system to deliver the electricity from a renewable energy facility to the contract customer.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4): 54-17-601
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(a): 54-17-601 "Renewable energy facility" means a renewable energy source as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(a)(i): is located in the state; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(a)(ii): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(a)(ii)(A): is located outside the state; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(a)(ii)(B): provides energy from baseload renewable resources.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(4)(b): "Renewable energy facility" does not include an electric generating facility for which the electric generating facility's costs are included in a qualified utility's rates as a facility that provides electric service to the qualified utility's system.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-801(5): "Renewable energy tariff" means a tariff offered by a qualified utility that allows the qualified utility to procure renewable generation on behalf of and to serve its customers.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802 Contracts for the purchase of electricity from a renewable energy facility.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(1): Within a reasonable time after receiving a request from a contract customer and subject to reasonable credit requirements, a qualified utility shall enter into a renewable energy contract with the requesting contract customer to supply some or all of the contract customer's electric service from one or more renewable energy facilities selected by the contract customer.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(2): Subject to a contract customer agreeing to pay the qualified utility for all incremental costs associated with metering facilities, communication facilities, and administration, a renewable energy contract may provide for electricity to be delivered to a contract customer:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(2)(a): from one renewable energy facility to a contract customer's single metered delivery location;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(2)(b): from multiple renewable energy facilities to a contract customer's single metered delivery location; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(2)(c): from one or more renewable energy facilities to a single contract customer's multiple metered delivery locations.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(3): (4); (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(3)(a): (4) A single contract customer may aggregate multiple metered delivery locations to satisfy the minimum megawatt limit under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(3)(b): (4) Multiple contract customers may not aggregate their separate metered delivery locations to satisfy the minimum megawatt limit under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(4): The amount of electricity provided to a contract customer under a renewable energy contract may not be less than 2.0 megawatts.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(5): The amount of electricity provided in any hour to a contract customer under a renewable energy contract may not exceed the contract customer's metered kilowatt-hour load in that hour at the metered delivery locations under the contract.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(6): (4); (4) A renewable energy contract that meets the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(7): The total amount of electricity to be generated by renewable energy facilities and delivered to contract customers at any one time under all renewable energy contracts may not exceed 300 megawatts, unless the commission approves in advance a higher amount.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-802(8): Chapter 15, Net Metering of Electricity Electricity generated by a renewable energy facility and delivered to a contract customer under a renewable energy contract may not be included in a net metering program under


Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-803 Ownership of a renewable energy facility -- Joint ownership -- Ownership of environmental attributes.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-803(1): (1)(a); (b); (c) A renewable energy facility may be owned:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-803(1)(a): by a person who will be a contract customer receiving electricity from the renewable energy facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-803(1)(b): by a qualified utility;

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805 Costs associated with delivering electricity from a renewable energy facility to a contract customer.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(1): To the extent that a renewable energy contract provides for the delivery of electricity from a renewable energy facility owned by the contract customer, the renewable energy contract shall require the contract customer to pay for the use of the qualified utility's transmission or distribution facilities at the qualified utility's applicable rates, which may include transmission costs at the qualified utility's applicable rate approved by the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(2): To the extent that a renewable energy contract provides for the delivery of electricity from a renewable energy facility owned by a person other than the qualified utility or the contract customer, the renewable energy contract shall require the contract customer to bear all reasonably identifiable costs that the qualified utility incurs in delivering the electricity from the renewable energy facility to the contract customer, including all costs to procure and deliver electricity and for billing, administrative, and related activities, as determined by the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(3): (1); (2); (2) A qualified utility that enters a renewable energy contract shall charge a contract customer for all metered electric service delivered to the contract customer, including generation, transmission, and distribution service, at the qualified utility's applicable tariff rates, excluding:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(3)(a): any kilowatt hours of electricity delivered from the renewable energy facility, based on the time of delivery, adjusted for transmission losses;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(3)(b): any kilowatts of electricity delivered from the renewable energy facility that coincide with the contract customer's monthly metered kilowatt demand measurement, adjusted for transmission losses;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(3)(c): (1); (2) any transmission and distribution service that the contract customer pays for under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-805(3)(d): (2) any transmission service that the contract customer provides under Subsection

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-901 Community Renewable Energy Act.
---------------------------------------------------------------
This part is known as the "Community Renewable Energy Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this part:Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(1)(a): "Auxiliary services" means those services necessary to safely and reliably:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(1)(a)(i): interconnect and transmit electric power from any renewable energy resource constructed or acquired for a community renewable energy program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(1)(a)(ii): integrate and supplement electric power from any renewable energy resource.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(1)(b): "Auxiliary services" shall include applicable Federal Energy Regulatory Commission requirements governing transmission and interconnection services.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(2): 54-1-1 "Commission" means the Public Service Commission created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(3): 54-17-904 "Community renewable energy program" means the program approved by the commission under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(4): "County" means the unincorporated area of a county.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(5): 54-4a-1 "Division" means the Division of Public Utilities created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(6): 54-17-909
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(6)(a): 54-17-909 "Initial opt-out period" means the period of time immediately after the community renewable energy program's commencement, as established by the commission by rule made pursuant to Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(6)(b): "Initial opt-out period" may not be shorter than three typical billing cycles of the qualified utility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(7): 10-1-104 "Municipality" means a city or a town as defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(8): 54-10a-101 "Office" means the Office of Consumer Services created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(9): "Ongoing costs" means the costs allocated to the state for transmission and distribution facilities, retail services, and generation assets that are not replaced assets.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(10): 54-17-903 "Participating community" means a municipality or a county:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(10)(a): whose residents are served by a qualified utility; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(10)(b): 54-17-903 the municipality or county meets the requirements in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(11): 54-17-905 "Participating customer" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(11)(a): a customer of a qualified utility located within the boundary of a municipality or county where a community renewable energy program has been approved by the commission; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(11)(b): 54-17-905 the customer has not exercised the right to not participate in the community renewable energy program as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(12): 54-17-801 "Qualified utility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(13): "Renewable electric energy supply" means incremental renewable energy resources that are developed to meet the equivalent of the annual electric energy consumption of participating customers within a participating community.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14): "Renewable energy resource" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(a): electric energy generated by a source that is naturally replenished and includes one or more of the following:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(a)(i): wind;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(a)(ii): solar photovoltaic or thermal solar technology;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(a)(iii): a geothermal resource; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(a)(iv): a hydroelectric plant; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(b): use of an energy efficient and sustainable technology the commission has approved for implementation that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(b)(i): increases efficient energy usage;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(b)(ii): is capable of being used for demand response; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(14)(b)(iii): facilitates the use and development of renewable generation resources through electrical grid management or energy storage.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(15): "Replaced asset" means an existing thermal energy resource:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(15)(a): that was built or acquired, in whole or in part, by a qualified utility to serve the qualified utility's customers, including customers within a participating community;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(15)(b): that was built or acquired prior to commission approval and the effective date of the community renewable energy program; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-17-902(15)(c): to the extent the asset is no longer used to serve participating customers.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 18 - Siting of High Voltage Power Line Act
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Siting of High Voltage Power Line Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(1): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Affected entity" means an entity as defined in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(2): "Affected landowner" means an owner of a property interest, as reflected in the most recent county or city tax records as receiving a property tax notice, whose property is located within a proposed corridor.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(a): "Construction" means the excavation, construction, and installation of a high voltage electric power line or upgraded high voltage transmission line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b): "Construction" does not include:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(i): the temporary use of sites; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii): studies and tests for:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii)(A): requirements of this chapter;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii)(B): state regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii)(C): federal regulations;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii)(D): securing geological and survey data; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(3)(b)(ii)(E): any other actions taken by a public utility reasonably necessary to determine the location of a target study area or proposed corridor.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(4): "High voltage power line" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(4)(a): an electrical high voltage power line with a nominal voltage of 230 kilovolts or more; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(4)(b): an upgraded high voltage power line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(5): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Land use application" has the same meaning as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(6): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Land use authority" has the same meaning as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(7): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Land use permit" has the same meaning as Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(8): 10-9a-103; 17-27a-103 "Legislative body" has the same meaning as provided in Sections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(9): "Proposed corridor" means the transmission line route within a target study area selected by the public utility as the public utility's proposed alignment for a high voltage power line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(10): "Proposed route" means the right-of-way needed for construction of the high voltage power line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(11): 54-2-1 "Public utility" has the same meaning as provided in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(12): "Target study area" means the geographic area for a new high voltage transmission line or an upgraded high voltage power line as proposed by a public utility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-18-102(13): "Upgraded high voltage power line" means increasing the voltage of an existing transmission line to 230 kilovolts or more.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 19 - Regulation of Internet Protocol Services
**************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Regulation of Internet Protocol Services."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this section:Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102(1): "Internet protocol-enabled service" means any service, functionality, or application that uses Internet protocol or a successor protocol that enables an end-user to send or receive voice, data, or video communications.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102(2): "Voice over Internet protocol service" means any service that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102(2)(a): enables real time, two-way voice communication originating from or terminating at the user's location in Internet protocol or a successor protocol;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102(2)(b): uses a broadband connection from the user's location; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-102(2)(c): permits a user to receive a telephone call that originates on the public switched telephone network and to terminate a call to the public switched telephone network.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103 Authority over Internet protocol-enabled services and voice over Internet protocol services.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(1): A state agency and political subdivision of the state may not, directly or indirectly, regulate Internet protocol-enabled service or voice over Internet protocol service.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2): (1); 54-8b-2.1 The regulatory prohibition in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(a): affect or limit the enforcement of criminal or civil laws, including consumer protection and unfair or deceptive trade practice laws, that apply to the conduct of business;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b): affect, limit, or prohibit the current or future assessment of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b)(i): a tax;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b)(ii): a 911 fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b)(iii): a universal service fund fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b)(iv): a telecommunication relay fee; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(b)(v): a public utility regulatory fee;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c): 54-8b-2.1 affect or modify:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c)(i): a right or obligation of any telecommunications carrier under 47 U.S.C. Sec. 251 and 47 U.S.C. Sec. 252;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c)(ii): any commission obligation to implement or enforce federal law;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c)(iii): a duty or power of the commission, under 47 U.S.C. Sec. 251 and 47 U.S.C. Sec. 252, including arbitration and enforcement of an interconnection agreement;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c)(iv): any obligation for the provision of video service by any person; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(c)(v): 54-8b-2.1 the application of Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-19-103(2)(d): affect the authority of the state or a political subdivision of the state to manage the use of a public right of way, including any requirement for the joint use of utility poles or other structures in the right of way.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-20-106 Extension of pilot program.
-----------------------------------------------------------
Before the first day of the legislative session in the final year of the pilot program period, the commission shall submit a report and recommendation to the Legislature regarding whether, in the discretion of the commission, the Legislature should, for the sustainable transportation and energy plan:Utah Code Annotated § 54-20-106(1): extend the plan or a portion of the plan as a ratepayer funded program;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-20-106(2): implement the plan or a portion of the plan as a state funded program; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-20-106(3): discontinue the plan or a portion of the plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-20-107 Other programs.
-----------------------------------------------
The commission may authorize a large-scale electric utility or a large-scale natural gas utility to establish a program in addition to the programs described in this chapter if the commission determines that the program is cost-effective and in the public interest.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 21 - Small Wireless Facilities Deployment Act
**************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(1): "Antenna" means communications equipment that transmits or receives an electromagnetic radio frequency signal used in the provision of a wireless service.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(2): Title 15A, State Construction and Fire Codes Act "Applicable codes" means the International Building Code, the International Fire Code, the National Electrical Code, the International Plumbing Code, and the International Mechanical Code, as adopted and amended under
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(3): "Applicable standards" means the structural standards for antenna supporting structures and antenna, known as ANSI/TIA-222, from the American National Standards Institute and the Telecommunications Industry Association.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(4): "Applicant" means a wireless provider who submits an application.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(5): "Application" means a request submitted by a wireless provider to an authority for a permit to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(5)(a): collocate a small wireless facility in a right-of-way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(5)(b): install, modify, or replace a utility pole or a wireless support structure.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6): (6)(a)(i); (vi)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a): (6)(a)(i); (vi) "Authority" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(i): the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(ii): a state agency;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(iii): a county;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(iv): a municipality;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(v): a town;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(vi): a metrotownship;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(vii): (6)(a)(i); (vi) a subdivision of an entity described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(viii): a special district or entity established to provide a single public service within a specific geographic area, including:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(viii)(A): a public utility district; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(a)(viii)(B): an irrigation district.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(6)(b): "Authority" does not include a state court having jurisdiction over an authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(7): "Authority pole" means a utility pole owned, managed, or operated by, or on behalf of, an authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(8): "Authority wireless support structure" means a wireless support structure owned, managed, or operated by, or on behalf of, an authority.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(9): "Category one authority" means a single authority with a population of 65,000 or greater.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(10): "Category two authority" means a single authority with a population of less than 65,000.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(11): "Collocate" means to install, mount, maintain, modify, operate, or replace a small wireless facility:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(11)(a): on a wireless support structure or utility pole; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(11)(b): for ground-mounted equipment, adjacent to a wireless support structure or utility pole.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(12): "Communications service" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(12)(a): a cable service, as defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 522(6);
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(12)(b): a telecommunications service, as defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 153(53);
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(12)(c): an information service, as defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 153(24); or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(12)(d): a wireless service.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(13): "Communications service provider" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(13)(a): a cable operator, as defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 522(5);
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(13)(b): a provider of information service, as information service is defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 153(24);
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(13)(c): a telecommunications carrier, as defined in 47 U.S.C. Sec. 153(51); or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(13)(d): a wireless provider.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14): "Decorative pole" means an authority pole:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(a): that is specially designed and placed for an aesthetic purpose; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b):

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(i)(A): a small wireless facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(i)(B): a specialty designed informational or directional sign; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(i)(C): a temporary holiday or special event attachment; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(ii): on which no appurtenance or attachment has been placed, other than:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(ii)(A): a small wireless facility;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(ii)(B): a specialty designed informational or directional sign; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(14)(b)(ii)(C): a temporary holiday or special event attachment.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(15): "Design district" means an area:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(15)(a): that is zoned or otherwise designated by municipal ordinance or code; and

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(21): "Micro wireless facility" means a type of small wireless facility:

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(21)(b): on which any exterior antenna is no longer than 11 inches; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-101(21)(c): that only provides Wi-Fi service.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102 Scope.
--------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(1): permits an entity to provide a service regulated under 47 U.S.C. Secs. 521 through 573, in a right-of-way without compliance with all applicable legal obligations;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(2): imposes a new requirement on the activity of a cable provider in a right-of-way for a cable service provided in this state;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(3): governs:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(3)(a): a pole that an electrical corporation owns or a wireless support structure that an electrical corporation owns; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(3)(b): the attachment of a small wireless facility to a pole that an electrical corporation owns or to a wireless support structure that an electrical corporation owns; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-102(4): confers on an authority any new jurisdiction over an electrical corporation.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103 Local authority jurisdiction.
-------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(1): (2) Subject to Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(2): An authority may exercise the authority's police-power-based regulations for the management of a public right-of-way:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(2)(a): on a nondiscriminatory basis to all users of the right-of-way;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(2)(b): to the extent of the authority's jurisdiction; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(2)(c): consistent with state and federal law.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(3): An authority may impose a regulation based on the authority's police power in the management of an activity of a wireless provider in a public right-of-way, if:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(3)(a): to the extent the authority enforces the regulation, the authority enforces the regulation on a nondiscriminatory basis; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(3)(b): the purpose of the regulation is to protect the health, safety, and welfare of the public.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(4): An authority may adopt design standards for the installation and construction of a small wireless facility or utility pole in a public right-of-way that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(4)(a): are reasonable and nondiscriminatory; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(4)(b): include additional installation and construction details that do not conflict with this chapter, including a requirement that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(4)(b)(i): an industry standard pole load analysis be completed and submitted to an authority, indicating that the utility pole, to which the small wireless facility is to be attached, will safely support the load; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(4)(b)(ii): small wireless facility equipment, on new and existing utility poles, be placed higher than eight feet above ground level.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(5): (4)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(5)(a): (4) A wireless provider shall comply with an authority's design standards described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(5)(b): An authority's obligations under this chapter may not be tolled or extended pending the adoption or modification of design standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(6): A wireless provider may not install a new utility pole in a public right-of-way without the authority's discretionary, nondiscriminatory, and written consent, if the public right-of-way is adjacent to a street or thoroughfare that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(6)(a): not more than 60 feet wide, as depicted in the official plat records; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(6)(b): adjacent to single-family residential lots, other multifamily residences, or undeveloped land that is designated for residential use by zoning or deed restrictions.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(7): Nothing in this chapter authorizes the state or any political subdivision, including an authority, to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(7)(a): require the deployment of a wireless facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(7)(b): regulate a wireless service.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-103(8): Except as provided in this chapter or otherwise specifically authorized by state law, an authority may not impose or collect a tax, fee, or charge on a communications service provider authorized to operate in a right-of-way for the provision of communications service over the communications service provider's communications facilities in the right-of-way.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-201 Applicability.
----------------------------------------------
This part only applies to a wireless provider deploying, within a right-of-way:Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-201(1): a small wireless facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-201(2): a utility pole associated with a small wireless facility.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-202 Prohibition on exclusive use.
-------------------------------------------------------------
An authority may not enter into an exclusive arrangement with any person for:Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-202(1): use of a right-of-way for the collocation of a small wireless facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-202(2): the installation, operation, marketing, modification, maintenance, or replacement of a utility pole.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-203 Right-of-way rates and fees.
------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-203(1): Part 5, Rates and Fees An authority may charge a wireless provider a rate or fee for the use of a right-of-way to collocate a small wireless facility, or to install, operate, modify, maintain, or replace a utility pole associated with the wireless provider's collocation of a small wireless facility, if the authority:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-203(1)(a): charges all other similarly situated wireless providers for use of the right-of-way; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-203(1)(b): Part 5, Rates and Fees charges only the rate or fee in accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-203(2): An authority may, on a nondiscriminatory basis, refrain from charging a rate or fee to a wireless provider for the use of a right-of-way.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204 Wireless provider right of access.
------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(1): 54-21-101(25)(b)(i); (ix) Subject to the provisions of this part, along, across, upon, or under a right-of-way, a wireless provider may, as a permitted use under the authority's zoning regulation and subject only to administrative review:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(1)(a): collocate a small wireless facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(1)(b): 54-21-101(25)(b)(i); (ix) install, operate, modify, maintain, or replace:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(1)(b)(i): a utility pole associated with the wireless provider's collocation of a small wireless facility; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(1)(b)(ii): 54-21-101(25)(b)(i); (ix) equipment described in Subsections
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(2): (1) A small wireless facility or utility pole under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(2)(a): obstruct or hinder the usual travel or public safety on a right-of-way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(2)(b): obstruct, damage, or interfere with:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(2)(b)(i): another utility facility in a right-of-way; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(2)(b)(ii): a utility's use of the utility's facility in a right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-204(3): Construction and maintenance by the wireless provider shall comply with all applicable legal obligations for the protection of underground and overhead utility facilities.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-205 Height limitations in a right-of-way.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-205(1): A new or modified utility pole that has a collocated small wireless facility, and that is installed in a right-of-way, may not exceed 50 feet above ground level.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-205(2): An antenna of a small wireless facility may not extend more than 10 feet above the top of a utility pole existing on or before September 1, 2018.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-206 Decorative poles.
-------------------------------------------------
If necessary to collocate a small wireless facility, a wireless provider may replace a decorative pole, if the replacement pole reasonably conforms to the design aesthetic of the displaced decorative pole.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207 Underground district.
-----------------------------------------------------
A wireless provider shall comply with an authority's prohibition on a communications service provider installing a structure in the right-of-way in an area designated solely for underground or buried cable and utility facilities, if:Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(1): the prohibition is reasonable and nondiscriminatory; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2): (2)(a)(i) the authority:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2)(a): (2)(a)(i)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2)(a)(i): requires that all cable and utility facilities, other than an authority pole and attachment, be placed underground; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2)(a)(ii): (2)(a)(i) establishes the requirement in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2)(b): does not prohibit the replacement of an authority pole in the designated area; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-207(2)(c): permits a wireless provider to seek a waiver, that is administered in a nondiscriminatory manner, of the undergrounding requirement for the placement of a new utility pole to support a small wireless facility.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-209 Manner of regulation.
-----------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-209(1): An authority shall manage a wireless provider's use of a right-of-way in a nondiscriminatory manner with regard to any other user of the right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-209(2): Any term or condition an authority imposes on a right-of-way user may not:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-209(2)(a): be unreasonable or discriminatory; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-209(2)(b): violate an applicable legal obligation or law.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210 Damage and repair.
--------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(1): If a wireless provider's activity causes damage to a right-of-way, the wireless provider shall repair the right-of-way to substantially the same condition as before the damage.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(2): (1) If a wireless provider fails to make a repair required by an authority under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(2)(a): make the required repair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(2)(b): charge the wireless provider the reasonable, documented, actual cost for the repair.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(3): (1) If the damage described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(3)(a): immediately make the necessary repair; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-210(3)(b): charge the wireless provider the reasonable, documented, actual cost for the repair.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-301 Applicability -- General.
---------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-301(1): This part applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-301(1)(a): the collocation of a small wireless facility in a right-of-way;

Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602 Noncompliant agreements and ordinances.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(1): An agreement or ordinance that does not fully comply with this chapter and applies to a small wireless facility or a utility pole that is operational or installed before May 11, 2018:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(1)(a): may not be renewed or extended unless the agreement is modified to fully comply with this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(1)(b): is invalid and unenforceable beginning November 8, 2018, unless the agreement or ordinance is modified before November 8, 2018, to fully comply with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(2): An agreement or ordinance entered into or passed before May 11, 2018, that does not fully comply with this chapter and applies to a small wireless facility or a utility pole that was not operational or installed before May 11, 2018, is invalid and unenforceable:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(2)(a): beginning May 11, 2018; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(2)(b): until the agreement or ordinance is modified to fully comply with this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(3): If an agreement or ordinance is invalid in accordance with this section, until an agreement or ordinance that fully complies with this chapter is entered or adopted:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(3)(a): a small wireless facility or a utility pole that is operational or installed before May 11, 2018, may remain installed and operate under the requirements of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-21-602(3)(b): a small wireless facility or utility pole may become operational or be installed in the right-of-way on or after May 11, 2018, under the requirements of this chapter.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 22 - Stray Current or Voltage Remediation Act
**************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101 Title -- Legislative findings.
--------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(1): This chapter is known as the "Stray Current or Voltage Remediation Act."
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2): The Legislature finds that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2)(a): to protect livestock and livestock operations, it is necessary and appropriate to establish an actionable level of stray current and voltage that is safely below any level that is capable of harming livestock or adversely affecting the behavior, health, or productivity of livestock;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2)(b): the efficient, effective, and safe generation, transmission, and distribution of electrical energy by electric entities is critical to the well-being of the citizens and the economy of the state;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2)(c): permitting an electric entity to face liability based on a level of stray current or voltage that is incapable of adversely affecting livestock seriously threatens the efficient, effective, and safe generation, transmission, and distribution of electrical energy in the state, as well as the continuing viability of economic activity that depends on electrical energy;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2)(d): to guarantee the sufficient availability of efficient, effective, and safe electrical energy in the state, which requires the continuing operation of electric entities, it is necessary and appropriate for the Legislature to establish a uniform actionable level for an electric entity with respect to stray current and voltage and livestock; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-101(2)(e): because the actionable level is set sufficiently below any level that is capable of adversely affecting the behavior, health, or productivity of livestock, any potential of harm to livestock from stray current or voltage below this level is highly remote and unexpected.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(1): "Actionable level" means stray current or voltage that is:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(1)(a): a steady-state, root mean square, alternating current (AC) of 2.0 milliamps or more through a 500 ohm resistor connected between livestock contact points, as measured by a digital true root mean square meter;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(1)(b): a steady-state, root mean square AC voltage of 1.0 volt or more across, in parallel with, a 500 ohm resistor connected between livestock contact points, as measured by a true root mean square meter;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(1)(c): a steady-state direct current (DC) of 2.8 milliamps or more through a 500 ohm resistor connected between livestock contact points, as measured by a digital meter; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(1)(d): a steady-state DC voltage of 1.4 volts or more across a 500 ohm resistor connected between livestock contact points, as measured by a digital meter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(2): (2)(a) "Electric entity" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(2)(a): an electrical corporation, independent energy producer, qualifying power producer, interlocal entity, public agency, or person engaged in generating, furnishing, transmitting, distributing, or marketing electrical power for public or private use; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(2)(b): (2)(a) an agent, affiliate, employee, or independent contractor of a person described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(3): 11-13-103 "Interlocal entity" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(4): "Livestock" means cattle, swine, sheep, equine, or poultry.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(5): "Livestock contact points" means two electrically conductive points that livestock may simultaneously contact.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(6): "Livestock operator" means a person who through an agreement with the owner of livestock has authority and is responsible to oversee the care and well being of the livestock.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(7): 11-13-103 "Public agency" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(8): "Qualified testing professional" means an electrical engineer who has:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(8)(a): graduated with an engineering degree from an accredited university;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(8)(b): completed no fewer than 40 hours of relevant stray current or voltage training, with electric utility experience; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(8)(c): been involved in at least one prior investigation involving the measurement or testing of stray current or voltage.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(9): "Root mean square" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(9)(a): a measure of the effective energy value of a wave or cycle; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(9)(b): for regularly shaped alternating current sine waves, a value of 0.707 multiplied by the peak value of the sine wave.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(10): "Steady-state" means:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(10)(a): for alternating current and AC voltage, a one minute average of root mean square amperage or voltage values, excluding transients; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(10)(b): for direct current and DC voltage, a one minute average of amperage or voltage values excluding transients.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(11): "Transient" means a current or voltage impulse:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(11)(a): lasting less than five thousandths of a second; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-102(11)(b): found on all types of electrical, data, and communications circuits.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-103 Scope of chapter.
-------------------------------------------------
This chapter does not expand or affect the jurisdiction of the commission. An electric entity is not subject to the jurisdiction of the commission unless made subject to the jurisdiction of the commission under a statute other than this chapter.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-201(2): To file a notice, a livestock owner or livestock operator shall provide written notice to the electric entity that documents:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-201(2)(a): the address of the livestock owner or livestock operator and the location of the potential stray current or voltage; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-201(2)(b): a description of the claimed impacts of the potential stray current or voltage.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-203 Liability limitations.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-203(1): An electric entity may not be held liable for damages or other relief if the claim for damages or other relief is based on livestock contact with any kind of stray current or voltage contributed by the electric entity below the actionable level.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-203(2): There is no presumption of liability if the stray current or voltage is equal to or greater than the actionable level.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-203(3): A claim for nuisance may not be asserted against an electric entity for damages due to stray current or voltage. Claims for stray current or voltage shall be limited to claims of negligence. The electric entity's conduct shall be evaluated using a standard of ordinary care under the circumstances.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-204 Committee review requirements.
--------------------------------------------------------------
By November 2020 and in three year intervals thereafter, the Public Utilities, Energy, and Technology Interim Committee shall review industry standards and peer reviewed research regarding levels of stray current and voltage and impacts to livestock.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-205 Disputes.
-----------------------------------------
A dispute under this chapter involving an electric entity shall be resolved as follows:Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-205(1): 54-7-9 if the electric entity is a public utility, in accordance with Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-22-205(2): if the electric entity is not a public utility, by filing an action with the district court.


Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 23 - Crossing Railroad Rights-of-way by Fiber Optic Carriers
*****************************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as "Crossing Railroad Rights-of-Way by Fiber Optic Carriers."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(1): "Consumer price index" means the Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers: All Items Less Food & Energy, as published by the Bureau of Labor Statistics of the United States Department of Labor.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a): "Crossing" means a telecommunications facility constructed under or across a railroad right-of-way:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a)(i): at an angle between 80 degrees and 100 degrees;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a)(ii): with a minimum depth of:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a)(ii)(A): 10 feet below rail level for nonhorizontal directional drilling; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a)(ii)(B): 15 feet below rail for horizontal directional drilling; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(a)(iii): within a county that is not a county of the first class.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(2)(b): "Crossing" does not include longitudinal occupancy of railroad right-of-way.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(3): "Facility" or "telecommunications facility" means fiber optics or related conduit installed in a crossing.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-102(4): "Fiber optic carrier" means a telecommunications corporation or a telecommunications corporation's contractor or agent.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103 Right-of-way crossing -- application for permission.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1): (1); 54-23-105
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(a): Any fiber optic carrier that intends to place a facility across or upon a railroad right-of-way shall submit a request for permission from the railroad prior to placing a facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b): (1); 54-23-105 A request under this Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b)(i): be in the railroad form of a completed crossing application;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b)(ii): include an engineering design that:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b)(ii)(A): shows the location of the proposed crossing and the railroad's property, tracks, and wires that the telecommunications facility will cross; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b)(ii)(B): conforms with guidelines published in the most recent edition of the National Electric Safety Code and American Railway Engineering and Maintenance-of-Way Association standards; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(1)(b)(iii): 54-23-105 include the standard crossing fee specified in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(2): Unless the railroad provides written or electronic notice to the fiber optic carrier that the proposed crossing is a serious threat to the safe operations of the railroad or to the current or future use of the railroad right-of-way, would violate any federal law or regulation applicable to a public transit district, or would violate an agreement between a public transit district and the federal government, the railroad shall approve the application within 35 calendar days after the receipt of a completed application for a crossing.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(3): This section applies to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(3)(a): any crossing in existence before May 14, 2019, if an agreement concerning the crossing has expired or has been terminated; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(3)(b): any crossing commenced on or after May 14, 2019.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-103(4): (3)(a); 54-23-105 If an applicant that intends to place a facility across or upon a railroad right-of-way at a crossing described in Subsection


Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-104 Right-of-way crossing -- Construction.
----------------------------------------------------------------------
Unless the railroad notifies the fiber optic carrier in writing or electronically that the approved crossing is a serious threat to the safe operation of the railroad or to the current or future use of the railroad right-of-way, would violate any federal law or regulation applicable to a public transit district, or would violate an agreement between a public transit district and the federal government, the railroad shall issue the permit or crossing agreement and schedule flagging to occur within 45 calendar days of the approved application.

Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105 Standard crossing fee.
------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(1): (5) Unless otherwise agreed by the parties, a fiber optic carrier that crosses a railroad right-of-way shall pay the railroad a one-time standard crossing fee of $1,250, adjusted as provided in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(2)(a): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the standard crossing fee is paid in lieu of any license, permit, application, processing fee, or any other fee or charge to reimburse the railroad for direct expenses incurred by the railroad as a result of the crossing.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(2)(b): Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, no other fee or charge related to the crossing may be assessed to the fiber optic carrier by the railroad.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(3): In addition to the standard crossing fee, the fiber optic carrier shall also reimburse the railroad for any reasonable and necessary flagging expense associated with a crossing, based on the railroad traffic at the crossing.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(4): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(4)(a): The placement of a single conduit is limited to a single applicant, and the conduit's contents are a single facility.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(4)(b): No additional fees are payable based on the individual fibers, wires, lines, or other items contained within a single conduit.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(5): (1) On January 1 of each year, the standard crossing fee under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(5)(a): one; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-105(5)(b): the actual percent change of the consumer price index during the most recent 12-month period for which data is available.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106 Objections -- petition to Public Service Commission by a railroad.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(1): If a railroad objects to the proposed crossing due to the proposal being a serious threat to the safe operations of the railroad or to the current or future use of the railroad right-of-way, a violation of any federal law or regulation applicable to a public transit district, or a violation of an agreement between a public transit district and the federal government, the railroad shall provide written or electronic notice to the fiber optic carrier of the objection and the specific basis for the objection.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(2)(a): If the parties make good faith efforts to resolve the objection, and are unable to resolve the objection, either party may petition the commission for assistance via mediation or arbitration of the disputed crossing application.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(2)(b): The petition shall be filed within 60 days of receipt of the objection.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(3): (2) If a petition is filed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(4): (3); Chapter 7, Hearings, Practice, and Procedure An order issued under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-106(5): The commission shall assess the costs associated with a petition equitably among the parties.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107 Objections -- petition to Public Service Commission by a fiber optic carrier.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(1): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(1)(a): If a railroad imposes additional requirements on a fiber optic carrier for crossing the railroad's lines, other than the proposed crossing being a serious threat to the safe operations of the railroad or to the current or future use of the railroad right-of-way, a violation of any federal law or regulation applicable to a public transit district, or a violation of an agreement between a public transit district and the federal government, the fiber optic carrier may object to one or more of the requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(1)(b): The fiber optic carrier shall provide written or electronic notice of the objection and the specific basis for the objection to the railroad.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(2): 
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(2)(a): If the parties make good faith efforts to resolve the objection, and are unable to resolve the objection, either party may petition the commission for resolution or modification of the additional requirements.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(2)(b): The petition shall be filed within 60 days of receipt of the objection.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(3): (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(3)(a): (2) If a petition is filed under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(3)(b): The commission shall issue an order within 120 days of filing of the petition.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(4): (3); Chapter 7, Hearings, Practice, and Procedure An order issued under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-107(5): The commission shall assess the costs associated with a petition equitably among the parties.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-23-108 Existing agreements.
----------------------------------------------------
Nothing in this chapter prevents a railroad and a fiber optic carrier from continuing under an existing agreement, or from otherwise negotiating the terms and conditions applicable to a crossing or the resolution of any disputes relating to the crossing.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 24 - Wildland Fire Planning and Cost Recovery Act
******************************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-101 Title.
--------------------------------------
This chapter is known as the "Wildland Fire Planning and Cost Recovery Act."

Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(1): "Electric cooperative" means an electrical corporation that is a:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(1)(a): distribution electrical cooperative; or
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(1)(b): wholesale electrical cooperative.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(2): 54-15-102 "Governing authority" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(3): 54-17-801 "Qualified utility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-102(4): "Wildland fire protection plan" means a plan submitted to the commission or governing authority in accordance with the requirements of this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-103 Commission rulemaking authority.
----------------------------------------------------------------
In accordance withUtah Code Annotated § 54-24-103(1): rules establishing procedures for the review and approval of a wildland fire protection plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-103(2): rules establishing the procedures for the review and approval of annual expenditures for the implementation of a wildland fire protection plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-103(3): any other rules that the commission determines are necessary to protect the public interest and implement this chapter.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201 Wildland fire protection plan for a qualified utility.
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(1): A qualified utility shall prepare a wildland fire protection plan in accordance with the requirements of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2): (1) A wildland fire protection plan under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(a): a description of areas within the service territory of the qualified utility that may be subject to a heightened risk of wildland fire;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(b): a description of the procedures, standards, and time frames that the qualified utility will use to inspect and operate its infrastructure;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(c): a description of the procedures and standards that the qualified utility will use to perform vegetation management;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(d): a description of proposed modifications or upgrades to facilities and preventative programs that the qualified utility will implement to reduce the risk of its electric facilities initiating a wildland fire;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(e): a description of procedures for de-energizing power lines and disabling reclosers to mitigate potential wildland fires taking into consideration:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(e)(i): the ability of the qualified utility to reasonably access the proposed power line to be de-energized;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(e)(ii): the balance of the risk of wildland fire with the need for continued supply of electricity to a community; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(e)(iii): any potential impact to public safety, first responders, and health and communication infrastructure;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(f): a description of the procedures the qualified utility intends to use to restore its electrical system in the event of a wildland fire;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(g): a description of the costs for the implementation of the plan, including system improvements and upgrades;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(h): a description of community outreach and public awareness efforts before and during a wildland fire season; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(2)(i): a description of potential participation, if applicable, with state or local wildland fire protection plans.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3): (3)(a); 65A-1-4; (3)(a)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(a): A qualified utility shall submit the wildland fire protection plan described in this section to the commission:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(a)(i): on or before June 1, 2020; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(a)(ii): on or before October 1 of every third year after calendar year 2020.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b): (3)(a); 65A-1-4 The commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b)(i): (3)(a) review the plan submitted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b)(ii): 65A-1-4 consider input from:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b)(ii)(A): 65A-1-4 the State Division of Forestry, Fire, and State Lands created in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b)(ii)(B): any other appropriate federal, state, or local entity that chooses to provide input; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(b)(ii)(C): other interested persons who choose to provide input.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(c): (3)(a) The commission shall approve a wildland fire protection plan submitted under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(c)(i): is reasonable and in the public interest; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(3)(c)(ii): appropriately balances the costs of implementing the plan with the risk of a potential wildland fire.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-201(4): No later than June 1, 2021, and each year after 2021, a qualified utility shall submit to the commission a report detailing the qualified utility's compliance with the qualified utility's wildland fire protection plan.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202 Cost recovery for wildland fire protection plan implementation.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202(1): A qualified utility shall recover in rates all prudently incurred investments and expenditures, including the costs of capital, made to implement an approved wildland fire protection plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202(2): 54-24-201 A qualified utility shall file an annual report to the commission identifying the actual capital investments and expenses made in the prior calendar year and a forecast of the capital investments and expenses for the present year to implement a wildland fire protection plan approved by the commission under Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202(3): The commission shall authorize the deferral and collection of the incremental revenue requirement for the capital investments and expenses:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202(3)(a): to implement an approved wildland fire protection plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-24-202(3)(b): not included in base rates.

Utah Code Annotated - Title 54 - Chapter 25 - Electrical Power Delivery Quality Act
***********************************************************************************

Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101 Definitions.
--------------------------------------------
As used in this chapter:Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101(1): "Electrical power delivery quality" means the suitability of power delivered to customers as measured in comparison to accepted industry standards on voltage and power quality.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101(2): "Electrical power delivery quality plan" means a plan submitted to the commission in accordance with the requirements of this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101(3): "Interconnection request" means a request from a utility-scale energy generation system to a qualified utility's transmission line.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101(4): 54-17-801 "Qualified utility" means the same as that term is defined in Section
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-101(5): "Utility-scale energy generation system" means an electric generation facility that has a generating capacity of more than two megawatts and is intermittent, non-dispatchable, or controlled by an inverter.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102 Commission rulemaking authority.
----------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(1): Title 63G, Chapter 3, Utah Administrative Rulemaking Act In accordance with
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(1)(a): rules establishing the submission of an electrical power delivery quality plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(1)(b): rules establishing procedures for the review of an electrical power delivery quality plan;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(1)(c): rules establishing the procedures for the review of the implementation of an electrical power delivery quality plan; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(1)(d): any other rules that the commission determines are necessary to protect the public interest and implement this chapter.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(2): (1) In establishing the procedures and rules described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(2)(a): qualified utilities;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(2)(b): utility-scale electricity providers; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-102(2)(c): other state agencies.


Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201 Electrical power delivery quality plan for a qualified utility.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(1): A qualified utility shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(1)(a): prepare an electrical power delivery quality plan in accordance with the requirements of this chapter; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(1)(b): submit the electrical power delivery quality plan to the commission.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2): (1); (2)(a) An electrical power delivery quality plan under Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2)(a): a description of the procedures and standards that the qualified utility will use to assess an interconnection request to:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2)(a)(i): decrease the risk that the interconnected utility-scale generation facility will adversely affect the electrical power delivery quality to other customers on the qualified utility lines; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2)(a)(ii): address adverse effects to the electrical power service quality caused by interconnected customer-owned generation systems that are discovered after the time of interconnection;
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2)(b): (2)(a) a description of the equipment that the qualified utility will use to perform the assessment described in Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(2)(c): a description of proposed modifications or upgrades to facilities and preventative programs that the qualified utility will implement to address any electrical power delivery quality issues that do not meet the qualified utility's interconnections policy or relevant national standards.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(3): (2)
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(3)(a): (2) The commission may only approve an electrical power delivery quality plan that meets the requirements of Subsection
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(3)(b): If the commission does not approve a proposed electrical power delivery quality plan, the commission shall:
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(3)(b)(i): notify the qualified utility that the proposed electrical power delivery quality plan was not approved; and
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(3)(b)(ii): provide specific recommendations to the qualified utility about changes needed for approval of the proposed electrical power delivery quality plan.
Utah Code Annotated § 54-25-201(4): On or before October 31, 2023, and before October 31 of each year after 2023, the commission shall report to the Public Utilities, Energy, and Technology Interim Committee regarding a qualified utility's compliance with the qualified utility's electrical power delivery quality plan.
